<div id="theReview">
<h2>Midnight in Paris</h2>
<p class="ratd"> Rated <em>PG</em></p>
<p><em>Review by David Stratton</em></p>
<p>Gil Pender, Owen Wilson, a Hollywood screenplay writer who would rather be a serious novelist, accompanies his pretty but shallow fiancee, Inez, RACHEL MCADAMS, on a holiday to Paris - her conservative and overbearing parents are also visiting the City of Light. <br/><br/>At night Gil, who if he had his way would like to live in Paris and who harbours romantic dreams of life there in the 1920s, strolls through Montmartre and is magically transported back to the time when writers like Ernest Hemingway and Scott Fitzgerald, composers like Cole Porter, artists like Dali and Picasso and filmmakers like Bunuel haunted the bars and cafes of this part of the city.<br/><br/>This appealing Woody Allen fantasy is somewhat in the mood of THE PURPLE ROSE OF CAIRO. Now that he's no longer, it seems, making films in his beloved Manhattan, his affectionate tributes to other great cities continue with this, which opens with a breathtaking sequence of images of Paris, worthy of a tourist promotional film, but evoking much the same mood as the opening of MANHATTAN. <br/><br/>Owen Wilson is well cast as the Allen surrogate, an artist doubtful of his talents, frustrated with his life. Rachel McAdams is asked to take on a rather thankless role as the shallow Inez, but the rest of the cast, including KATHY BATES as Gertrude Stein and MARION COTILLARD as Adriana, Picasso's mistress, are excellent. This combination of whimsy and romance is, for me, much more successful than Allen's previous European city film, VICKY CRISTINA BARCELONA.</p>
<h2>Further comments</h2>
<p>DAVID: Margaret, what did you think?<br/><br/>MARGARET: He wears his heart on his sleeve with this one, doesn't he?<br/><br/>DAVID: He does.<br/><br/>MARGARET: That opening sequence, it's sort of like he can't tear himself away from being in love with the city. <br/><br/>DAVID: Yes, it's a lovely opening.<br/><br/>MARGARET: It's gorgeous, and that travelling back in time... it's such whimsy but it actually works. <br/><br/>DAVID: It does.<br/><br/>MARGARET: It's where we all wanted to be... Paris at that particular time with all those people.<br/><br/>DAVID: Although the irony is that...<br/><br/>MARGARET: Yes, I know, they want to be...<br/><br/>DAVID: Back in the previous epoch, yes.<br/><br/>MARGARET: My only problem with Woody Allen these days is the Rachel McAdams character, Inez, is so unflatteringly drawn. I've got antennae up now for the way Woody Allen writes women.<br/><br/>DAVID: Unfairly. Unfairly.<br/><br/>MARGARET: I know, I know. But he's just got a bee in his bonnet about women being horrible.<br/><br/>DAVID: But she had to be unsympathetic so that he can go off on these - that's part of the plot, Margaret.<br/><br/>MARGARET: Well, no, it's sort of like why is he with her if she's so shallow and ridiculous?<br/><br/>DAVID: She's lovely. She's beautiful.<br/><br/>MARGARET: No. No. No. But at the same time it's, for me, the most acceptable Woody Allen film in a long time.<br/><br/>DAVID: Acceptable, good.<br/><br/>MARGARET: Acceptable. I'm giving it three and a half stars.<br/><br/>DAVID: I liked it a lot. I'm giving it four.</p>

Always interesting to see that many of the negative reactions to movies on this site usually use bad grammar or rude language. Why is it that people cannot critique with manners and intelligence? Interesting too that most of these people despise the clever films so much. Cheers to great cinema I say!</br></p>

<h3>Ben :</h3>
<p class="date">26 Oct 2012 10:59:07am</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[10]]<br>Overall, this is a well written, fun, light hearted and entertaining flick to see, with a quirky, non scientific take on time travel that is refreshingly different. It's one flaw, and a substantial one at that - is the characterisation of Inez as this shallow, ignorant, typical American tourist. McAdams does well in what is a very unflattering role. Other then that, it's difficult to fault this one.<br><br>6.5/10 from me.</br></br></br></p>
<p class="links">

<h3>Leigh :</h3>
<p class="date">06 Apr 2012 3:48:55pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[7]]<br>I didn't think it were possible that I could be more keen to see Paris than I already was, until I saw Paris by midnight, in Midnight in Paris! Affectionately brought to life by a faultless screenplay and carefully, yet beautifully photographed, this is Woody Allen's finest work on paper and screen since 2005's masterpiece 'Matchpoint'. Once again, all characters introduced are of significant relevance, regardless of how much screen time is given, to aid the main man on his journey to truly discovering himself which makes for an always absolutely pleasant and delightful viewing experience.</br></p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229133413/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=14336&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d379%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay12081_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m12081"></a>
<h3>Michael D. Mueller :</h3>
<p class="date">08 Jan 2012 1:30:57am</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[10]]<br>The light whimsical touch of this wonderful film balances an emotional depth.  Is Woody Allen also looking back on his own life, to his early years as a writer, when he might have turned his genius to literature?  Does he, like Gil, consider himself (back then) a Hollywood hack?  The movie is perfect for Owen Wilson, giving him an intelligent role, within which a searching character comes to understand and accept himself.  Kathy Bates is superb (an Oscar-worthy performance) and Marion Cotillard is gorgeous and powerfully present, like great art, speaking to the eyes and heart.  Illuminating and magical.</br></p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229133413/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=12081&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d379%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<p class="date">31 Dec 2011 3:26:22am</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[8]]<br>I watched this flight on a recent flight to Australia and loved it so much I couldn't wait to watch it again on the flight back! Simply put, it's a romantic film, a romance with Paris. It's about following your dreams and being swept up in the city and place that resonates with you. With the time-travel and famous people from the past it is all fantasy. But if you identify with its romantic sentiment then I think you will really enjoy this film. Technically (character development, a warts-and-all depiction of Paris etc). you will probably find faults.</br></p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229133413/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=11914&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d379%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[9]]<br>Being the world's biggest woody Allen fan would make me somewhat biased in writing this. But having said that, I have seen all his films so I am more critical of what he puts out. This film included all of woody's staples, frustrated men, highly strung women, romantic European cities, magical escapism. It's his best film for a while for sure, but still not "Annie hall" or "manhattan". But still, woody is better than most at knowing what makes a good romantic comedy. A true genius!</br></p>

<h3>David :</h3>
<p class="date">28 Nov 2011 12:04:27pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[10]]<br/>A triumph. So inspiring that a 75yo can get out of bed, let alone write &amp; direct a brilliant film. Who else could persuade 3 Oscar winners (Bates, Brody, Cotillard) plus the French First Lady to take relatively minor support roles! Such a welcome relief from Scorcese's grimness &amp; Apatow's grossness. Possibly 30 actors, most of whom I've never heard of, contributed to this masterpiece, and not one false note from any of them. As he's already done in Barcelona and London!<br/><br/>The film when it finally begins, is a messy reworking of a story he wrote 40-odd years ago in which Madame Bovary is magicked into 20th century New York.<br/><br/>This one, however, consists almost entirely of people saying "Hello, I'm Picasso/Hemingway/Gertrude Stein" in lieu of a plot.<br/><br/>It's all so tedious and dreadful, and our reviewers are ready for retirement if they thought otherwise.</p>

<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[10]]<br/>What  an incredible experience this amazing movie turned out to be. <h3>Maryann :</h3>
<p class="date">31 Oct 2011 1:42:15pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[8]]<br/>I agree with David that this film is reminiscent of The Purple Rose of Cairo, another Woody Allen film I loved. Both films set up a completely implausible premise which is so whimsical and charming you just can't help but be drawn into it. And I think part of its charm is that Allen doesn't explain the why or the how, he just takes the idea and runs with it. This film is a beautiful tribute to a gorgeous city that attracted and inspired so many great artists. Who wouldn't want to trawl the streets of Paris with them?</p>

<h3>John :</h3>
<p class="date">26 Oct 2011 10:45:40pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[8]]<br/>for me, the most important revelation was the advice Gertrude Stein gave Gil about his novel and the role of the artist. It seemed to foreshadow the ending of the film. Hemingway was at times comic but also hypnotic and his remarks about truth seemed to resonate throughout...we know that the relationship between gil and inez is doomed but it's the dramatic irony that keeps it interesting... It's a story about the journey to self awareness. Woody Allen is so great with little details too. Sometimes the funniest lines are the ones you might miss if you're not paying attention.</p>

<h3>Inez :</h3>
<p class="date">26 Oct 2011 12:08:20pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[10]]<br/>ollowing the previous comment and addressing Margaret's question: Why would our protagonist put up with her shallowness?For any of the many reasons we have all stayed in meaningless relationships; to inevitably question our own dissatisfaction in order to further realize what we truly need.<br/><br/>Ironically, through this interpretation Margaret has further demonstrated precisely the satirical point Allen has so cleverly made, and once again its Woody who gets the last laugh! <a id="m_ucMessageDisplay10780_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m10780"></a>
<h3>benny :</h3>
<p class="date">26 Oct 2011 7:44:35am</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[10]]<br/>Addressing Margaret's misreading of Allen's female characters, through which Allen does seem to pour not only his frustration, but the frustrations of all artist who have attempting to express a vision and had it suffocated before it's had a chance to breath. To interpret the character's gender as a stance against women, is to apply a political agenda upon a cultural dilemma, and therefore to miss the satirical point. Having a bee in the bonnet has always been healthy impetus for creative work, but in this case,  perhaps it worth asking the question, who's bonnet is the bee really in?</p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229133413/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=10780&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d379%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<h3>waldo :</h3>
<p class="date">24 Oct 2011 11:49:18pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[9]]<br/>With WA films, the bad are a big fall from the superb. Thankfully, his ode to love, art and Paris is flawlessly executed. Under his direction, the actors are stong, intuitive and authentic, even (astoundingly) Madame Bruni.<br/>Allen's strongest suit is subtlety and though this is an unembarrassed homage to Paree, it's not exaggerated. The City of Romance deserves to be wooed and Woody takes his time like all lovers should.<br/>As for Marg's inflammatory insinuation about Allen's supposed misogyny, tch. Women cast as his central characters are always honestly portrayed and never look more beautiful than in his lens.</p>

<li>
<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay10708_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m10708"></a>
<h3>Virgil Starkwell :</h3>
<p class="date">23 Oct 2011 2:02:12am</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[9]]<br/>Yes, it is indulgent, sentimental, rife with Allen's tropes and at times a film whose images are more akin to a travelogue than a romantic comedy. However this is easily one of Allen's nest efforts. with so much to laugh at and with, as well as muse upon some poignant observations about life, love, art and death.  Some would argue that Allen lost his mojo after Deconstructing Harry...if he did he's got it back in spades here. Highly recommended</p>
<p class="links">

<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay10668_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m10668"></a>
<h3>Daniel Spicer :</h3>
<p class="date">20 Oct 2011 10:10:42pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Midnight in Paris))[[10]]<br/>There's a bit of romance, but this movie is mainly about novelty and nostalgia. Woody Allen writes and directs a very enjoyable story because it's original and smart. It's incredibly well-paced and so short. The dialogue is insane, well-stated and crisp. The whole movie encompasses a pleasant stroll through Paris; it's a genre bender with a touch of sci-fi. It's amusing and at times funny, especially the best scene involving Inez's missing ear rings. I thought the movie was so enjoyable and mesmerising. It really takes you to Paris.</p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229133413/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=10668&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d379%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<script language="JavaScript" type="text/javascript">


var newtopicKey;

$(document).ready(function(){

audShow();
changeAction();
formatComments();

// end ready
});	

function audShow() {
	// display word count only if js enabled
	document.getElementById("wordCount").style.display='inline';
	document.getElementById("audiencecomment").style.display='block';
	if (document.getElementById("allnewComments")) {
		document.getElementById("allnewComments").innerHTML = document.getElementById("loadComments").innerHTML;
	}
}


function changeAction() {
	// avoids non-js form submission 
	var tmpStoryid = "??StoryID??";
	if (document.m_frmMainForm) {
		document.m_frmMainForm.action = 'https://web.archive.org/web/20141229133413/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/NewMessage.aspx?b=117&amp;tn='+tmpStoryid+'&amp;dm=1&amp;tpa=&amp;r=&amp;layout=popup';
		}
}



function formatComments() {
	// replace H3 tag with 'Name:' + name
	var arrayH3 = document.getElementById("comments").getElementsByTagName("h3");
	for (var i = 0; i < arrayH3.length; i++) {
		var theString = arrayH3[i].innerHTML;
		theString = theString.replace(":", "");
		theString = "Name: "+theString;
		arrayH3[i].innerHTML = 	theString;
	}
	// add rating value to each comment
	var arrayComment = getElementsByClassName( 'comment', 'p' );	
	for (var c = 0; c < arrayComment.length; c++) {
		var theComment = arrayComment[c].innerHTML;
		theComment = theComment.replace("[[", "<span class='userRating'>Rating: <img src='https://web.archive.org/web/20141229133413/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/audience/stars").replace("]]",".png' alt='rating'></span>").replace("((", "<!-- ").replace(")))", "))").replace("))", "-->");
		arrayComment[c].innerHTML = theComment;
	}

	
}


function formCheck(zeForm) {
	// pass key to form
	document.getElementById("keyField").value = newtopicKey;
	// basic validation
	if (document.getElementById("yname").value.length < 1) {
		alert("Please enter your name or nickname.");
		document.getElementById("yname").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;
	}
	if (document.getElementById("yemail").value.length < 6) {
		alert("Please enter a valid email address.");
		document.getElementById("yemail").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;
	}
	if (zeForm.score.options[0].selected && zeForm.score.options[0].value=="na") {
		alert("You forgot to rate the movie!");
		document.getElementById("score").style.background='#FFFDC8';	
		return false;
	}	
	// check for http
	spamcheck=zeForm.m_tbxText.value;
	if (spamcheck.indexOf("http")!=-1) {
		document.m_frmMainForm.action = 'https://web.archive.org/web/20141229133413/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/audience/blank.htm';
	}
	// check word count
	wct = cnt(zeForm.m_tbxText.value);
	if (wct > 100) {
		alert("Comments are limited to 100 words. You've written "+wct+" words!");
		document.getElementById("remark").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;	
	}
	
	// replace usual suspect bad characters 
	badChars = Array  ('', '', '', '', '', 'ö', 'é', 'è', 'ñ', 'â', ' ', '','','´');
	goodChars = Array ('...', '-', '-', '"', '"', 'o', 'e', 'e', 'n', 'a', ' ', '\'','\'','\'');
	fld = document.getElementById("remark");
	for(i=0;i<badChars.length;i++){
		restring = new RegExp( badChars[i] , 'g');
		fld.value = fld.value.replace(restring,goodChars[i]);
	}
	fldn = document.getElementById("yname");
	for(j=0;j<badChars.length;j++){
		restringj = new RegExp( badChars[j] , 'g');
		fldn.value = fldn.value.replace(restringj,goodChars[j]);
	}	
	
	// add rating to comment field in [[ ]] tags 
	var theSel = zeForm.score.selectedIndex;
	var theRating = zeForm.score[theSel].value; 
	zeForm.m_tbxText.value = "[["+theRating+"]]\n" + zeForm.m_tbxText.value;
	
	// add movie title to comment field in (( )) tags 
	zeForm.m_tbxText.value = "(("+theMovie+"))" + zeForm.m_tbxText.value;	
	
	// display thankyou div layer and hide form. 
	document.getElementById("favFormThx").style.display='block';
	document.getElementById("favForm").style.display='none';
	document.getElementById("wordCount").style.display='none';	
	
	// all clear, submit the form
	return true;
}

// word count function
function cnt(theform){
	var y=theform;
	var r = 0;
	a=y.replace('\n',' ');
	a=a.split(' ');
	for (z=0; z<a.length; z++) {if (a[z].length > 0) r++;}
	return r;
}

function remainingWords(textAreaContent,textAreaContentValue, maxWords) 
{
	// Determine the number of words we have left
	var numberofwords = cnt(textAreaContentValue);
	wordsLeft = maxWords - numberofwords;
	if (wordsLeft < 1)
	{	// if 100 change color to red
		document.getElementById("wcNum").style.color='red'; 
	} else {
		document.getElementById("wcNum").style.color='#ffffff'; 
	}
	// update word count number
	document.getElementById("wcNum").innerHTML=(0+numberofwords);
}

// windows media alt box
function showWindows() {
	document.getElementById("windowsMed").style.display='block';
}


// generic get by class name
function getElementsByClassName(strClass, strTag, objContElm) {
  strTag = strTag || "*";
  objContElm = objContElm || document;    
  var objColl = objContElm.getElementsByTagName(strTag);
  if (!objColl.length &&  strTag == "*" &&  objContElm.all) objColl = objContElm.all;
  var arr = new Array();                              
  var delim = strClass.indexOf('|') != -1  ? '|' : ' ';   
  var arrClass = strClass.split(delim);    
  for (var i = 0, j = objColl.length; i < j; i++) {                         
    var arrObjClass = objColl[i].className.split(' ');   
    if (delim == ' ' && arrClass.length > arrObjClass.length) continue;
    var c = 0;
    comparisonLoop:
    for (var k = 0, l = arrObjClass.length; k < l; k++) {
      for (var m = 0, n = arrClass.length; m < n; m++) {
        if (arrClass[m] == arrObjClass[k]) c++;
        if ((delim == '|' && c == 1) || (delim == ' ' && c == arrClass.length)) {
          arr.push(objColl[i]); 
          break comparisonLoop;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  return arr; 
}

// called from 'new discussion' page in iframe
function sayHello(theKey) {
	newtopicKey = theKey;
}

// talk to www2b iframe
document.domain = "abc.net.au";

		//mobile device supports m3u8 html5 HLS video

	}
	else {
		//desktop browsers flash

	} 	
			
	
// end ready
});
